</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Subphylum of chordates</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">


</p>

</tbody></table><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1289143401">@media(max-width:640px){body:not(.skin-minerva) .mw-parser-output .infobox{width:100%!important}body:not(.skin-minerva) .mw-parser-output .infobox th{width:50%}}@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota tr{background:transparent!important}html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota img{background:transparent}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota tr{background:transparent!important}html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .infobox.biota img{background:white}}.mw-parser-output .infobox.biota .taxobox-edit-taxonomy img{background:transparent!important}body.skin-vector .mw-parser-output table.biota.infobox{margin-top:0.5em}body.skin--responsive .mw-parser-output table.biota.infobox tr.taxonrow2 td{padding:2px 10px}</style>
<p><b>Vertebrates</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/ɜːr/: &#39;ur&#39; in &#39;fur&#39;">ɜːr</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>),<sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> also called <b>craniates</b>, are <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">animals</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_column" class="mw-redirect" title="Vertebral column">vertebral column</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Cranium" class="mw-redirect" title="Cranium">cranium</a>. The vertebral column surrounds and protects the <a href="/wiki/Spinal_cord" title="Spinal cord">spinal cord</a>, while the cranium protects the <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">brain</a>. 
</p><p>The vertebrates make up the <a href="/wiki/Subphylum" title="Subphylum">subphylum</a> <b>Vertebrata</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/ɜːr/: &#39;ur&#39; in &#39;fur&#39;">ɜːr</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">VUR</span>-tə-<span style="font-size:90%">BRAY</span>-tə</i></a>) with some 65,000 species, by far the largest ranked grouping in the <a href="/wiki/Phylum" title="Phylum">phylum</a> <a href="/wiki/Chordata" class="mw-redirect" title="Chordata">Chordata</a>. The vertebrates include <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a>, and various classes of <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptiles</a>. The fish include the jawless <a href="/wiki/Agnatha" title="Agnatha">Agnatha</a>, and the jawed <a href="/wiki/Gnathostomata" title="Gnathostomata">Gnathostomata</a>. The jawed fish include both the <a href="/wiki/Chondrichthyes" title="Chondrichthyes">cartilaginous fish</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Osteichthyes" title="Osteichthyes">bony fish</a>. Bony fish include the <a href="/wiki/Sarcopterygii" title="Sarcopterygii">lobe-finned fish</a>, which gave rise to the <a href="/wiki/Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod">tetrapods</a>, the animals with four limbs. Despite their success, vertebrates still only make up less than five percent of all described <a href="/wiki/Animal_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Animal species">animal species</a>.
</p><p>The first vertebrates appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Cambrian_explosion" title="Cambrian explosion">Cambrian explosion</a> some 518 million years ago. Jawed vertebrates evolved in the <a href="/wiki/Ordovician" title="Ordovician">Ordovician</a> or <a href="/wiki/Silurian" title="Silurian">Silurian</a>; bony fishes appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Silurian" title="Silurian">Silurian</a> and diversified widely in the <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a>. The first <a href="/wiki/Tetrapods" class="mw-redirect" title="Tetrapods">tetrapods</a> appeared towards the end of the  <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a>, and the first amphibians appeared on land in the <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous">Carboniferous</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaurs</a> appeared, the latter giving rise to <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a>. Extant species are roughly equally divided between fishes of all kinds, and <a href="/wiki/Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod">tetrapods</a>. Populations of many species have been in steep decline since 1970 because of  <a href="/wiki/Land-use_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Land-use change">land-use change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Overexploitation" title="Overexploitation">overexploitation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> and the impact of <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive species</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Characteristics">Characteristics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Characteristics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Unique_features">Unique features</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Unique features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Vertebrates belong to <a href="/wiki/Chordate" title="Chordate">Chordata</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Phylum" title="Phylum">phylum</a> characterised by five <a href="/wiki/Synapomorphies" class="mw-redirect" title="Synapomorphies">synapomorphies</a> (unique characteristics): namely a <a href="/wiki/Notochord" title="Notochord">notochord</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Dorsal_nerve_cord" title="Dorsal nerve cord">hollow nerve cord along the back</a>, a post-anal tail, an <a href="/wiki/Endostyle" title="Endostyle">endostyle</a> (often as a <a href="/wiki/Thyroid" title="Thyroid">thyroid</a> gland), and pharyngeal <a href="/wiki/Gill" title="Gill">gills</a> arranged in pairs. Vertebrates share these characteristics with other chordates.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>Vertebrates are distinguished from all other animals, including other chordates, by multiple synapomorphies, namely: a vertebral column; a skull of bone or cartilage; a large brain divided into 3 or more sections; a muscular heart with multiple chambers; an inner ear with <a href="/wiki/Semicircular_canals" title="Semicircular canals">semicircular canals</a>; sense organs including the eyes, ears, and nose; and digestive organs including the intestines, liver, pancreas, and stomach.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Farina&#95;2018&#95;5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farina_2018-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Physical">Physical</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Physical"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fish_anatomy" title="Fish anatomy">Fish anatomy</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Vertebrate_body_plan.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vertebrate_body_plan.svg/1280px-Vertebrate_body_plan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="1000" height="236" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Vertebrate_body_plan.svg/3840px-Vertebrate_body_plan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="302" /></a><figcaption>Idealised vertebrate body plan, showing key characteristics</figcaption></figure>
<p>Vertebrates (and other chordates) belong to the <a href="/wiki/Bilateria" title="Bilateria">Bilateria</a>, a group of animals with mirror symmetrical bodies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They move, typically by swimming, using <a href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">muscles</a> along the back, supported by a strong but flexible <a href="/wiki/Skeleton" title="Skeleton">skeletal</a> structure, the spine or <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_column" class="mw-redirect" title="Vertebral column">vertebral column</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Romer&#95;1977&#95;7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romer_1977-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The name 'vertebrate' derives from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">vertebratus</i></span>, 'jointed',<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> from <i><a href="/wiki/Vertebra" title="Vertebra">vertebra</a></i>, 'joint', in turn from Latin <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">vertere</i></span>, 'to turn'.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-MW2024&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MW2024-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Naturkundemuseum_Berlin_-_Dinosaurierhalle.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Naturkundemuseum_Berlin_-_Dinosaurierhalle.jpg/500px-Naturkundemuseum_Berlin_-_Dinosaurierhalle.jpg" decoding="async" width="500" height="138" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Naturkundemuseum_Berlin_-_Dinosaurierhalle.jpg/1280px-Naturkundemuseum_Berlin_-_Dinosaurierhalle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3622" data-file-height="1000" /></a><figcaption>Fossilized skeleton (cast) of <i><a href="/wiki/Diplodocus_carnegii" class="mw-redirect" title="Diplodocus carnegii">Diplodocus carnegii</a></i>, showing an extreme example of the <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_column" class="mw-redirect" title="Vertebral column">vertebral column</a> that gives the vertebrates their name. The species is a <a href="/wiki/Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod">tetrapod</a>, its four legs adapting the fish-like body plan for walking on land. The specimen is 26&#160;m (85&#160;ft) long.</figcaption></figure>
<p>As embryos, vertebrates still have a notochord. In all but the <a href="/wiki/Agnatha" title="Agnatha">jawless fishes</a>, it is replaced with a vertebral column (made of <a href="/wiki/Bone" title="Bone">bone</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cartilage" title="Cartilage">cartilage</a>) during development.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Romer&#95;1977&#95;7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romer_1977-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Vertebrate embryos have <a href="/wiki/Pharyngeal_arch" title="Pharyngeal arch">pharyngeal arches</a>; in adult <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>, these support the <a href="/wiki/Gill" title="Gill">gills</a>, while in adult <a href="/wiki/Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod">tetrapods</a> they develop into other structures.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-dev&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dev-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Graham2001&#95;11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Graham2001-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Embryonic_development" class="mw-redirect" title="Embryonic development">In the embryo</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Neural_plate" title="Neural plate">layer of cells</a> along the back <a href="/wiki/Neurulation" title="Neurulation">folds and fuses</a> into a hollow <a href="/wiki/Neural_tube" title="Neural tube">neural tube</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Martín-Durán&#95;2018&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martín-Durán_2018-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This develops into the <a href="/wiki/Spinal_cord" title="Spinal cord">spinal cord</a>, and at its front end, the <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">brain</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Martín-Durán&#95;2018&#95;12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martín-Durán_2018-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The brain receives information about the world through nerves which carry signals from <a href="/wiki/Sense_organ" class="mw-redirect" title="Sense organ">sense organs</a> in the skin and body.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Because the ancestors of vertebrates usually moved forwards, the front of the body encountered stimuli before the rest of the body, favouring <a href="/wiki/Cephalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Cephalisation">cephalisation</a>, the evolution of a head containing sense organs and a brain to process the sensory information.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Brusca&#95;2016&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brusca_2016-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Vertebrates have a tubular <a href="/wiki/Gastrointestinal_tract" title="Gastrointestinal tract">gut</a> that extends from the <a href="/wiki/Mouth" title="Mouth">mouth</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Anus" title="Anus">anus</a>. The vertebral column typically continues beyond the anus to form an elongated  <a href="/wiki/Tail" title="Tail">tail</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Handrigan&#95;2003&#95;15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handrigan_2003-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Holland&#95;2015&#95;16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holland_2015-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Hejnol&#95;2015&#95;17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hejnol_2015-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Gills_(esox).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Gills_%28esox%29.jpg/250px-Gills_%28esox%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="178" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Gills_%28esox%29.jpg/500px-Gills_%28esox%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2080" data-file-height="1847" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Branchial_arch" title="Branchial arch">Branchial arches</a> bearing <a href="/wiki/Gill" title="Gill">gills</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Northern_pike" title="Northern pike">pike</a> </figcaption></figure>
<p>The ancestral vertebrates, and most extant species, are <a href="/wiki/Aquatic_animal" title="Aquatic animal">aquatic</a> and carry out <a href="/wiki/Gas_exchange" title="Gas exchange">gas exchange</a> in their gills. The gills are finely-branched structures which bring the blood close to the water. They are positioned just behind the head, supported by cartilaginous or bony <a href="/wiki/Branchial_arch" title="Branchial arch">branchial arches</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Jawed_vertebrate" class="mw-redirect" title="Jawed vertebrate">jawed vertebrates</a>, the first gill arch pair evolved into the jaws.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a> and some primitive bony fishes, the larvae have <a href="/wiki/External_gills" title="External gills">external gills</a>, branching off from the gill arches.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">Oxygen</a> is carried from the gills to the body in the <a href="/wiki/Blood" title="Blood">blood</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> is returned to the gills, in a closed <a href="/wiki/Circulatory_system" title="Circulatory system">circulatory system</a> driven by a chambered <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod">tetrapods</a> have lost the gills of their fish ancestors; they have adapted the <a href="/wiki/Swim_bladder" title="Swim bladder">swim bladder</a> (that fish use for buoyancy) into <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">lungs</a> to breathe air, and the circulatory system is adapted accordingly.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gaining&#95;ground&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaining_ground-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the same time, they adapted the bony fins of the <a href="/wiki/Sarcopterygii" title="Sarcopterygii">lobe-finned fishes</a> into two pairs of walking <a href="/wiki/Leg" title="Leg">legs</a>, carrying the weight of the body via the <a href="/wiki/Appendicular_skeleton" title="Appendicular skeleton">shoulder and pelvic girdles</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gaining&#95;ground&#95;22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gaining_ground-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>Vertebrates vary in size from the smallest <a href="/wiki/Frog" title="Frog">frog</a> species such as <i><a href="/wiki/Brachycephalus_pulex" title="Brachycephalus pulex">Brachycephalus pulex</a></i>, with a minimum adult <a href="/wiki/Snout%E2%80%93vent_length" title="Snout–vent length">snout–vent length</a> of 6.45 millimetres (0.254&#160;in)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-smallest&#95;vertebrate&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smallest_vertebrate-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to the <a href="/wiki/Blue_whale" title="Blue whale">blue whale</a>, at up to 33&#160;m (108&#160;ft) and weighing some 150 tonnes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Molecular">Molecular</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Molecular"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Molecular_marker" title="Molecular marker">Molecular markers</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Conserved_signature_indels" title="Conserved signature indels">conserved signature indels</a> in <a href="/wiki/Protein_sequence" class="mw-redirect" title="Protein sequence">protein sequences</a> have been identified and provide distinguishing criteria for the vertebrate subphylum.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gupta&#95;2016&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gupta_2016-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Five molecular markers are exclusively shared by all vertebrates and reliably distinguish them from all other animals; these include protein synthesis <a href="/wiki/Elongation_factor-2" class="mw-redirect" title="Elongation factor-2">elongation factor-2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eukaryotic_translation_initiation_factor_3" class="mw-redirect" title="Eukaryotic translation initiation factor 3">eukaryotic translation initiation factor 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adenosine_kinase" title="Adenosine kinase">adenosine kinase</a> and a protein related to <a href="/wiki/Ubiquitin_carboxyl-terminal_hydrolase" class="mw-redirect" title="Ubiquitin carboxyl-terminal hydrolase">ubiquitin carboxyl-terminal hydrolase</a>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gupta&#95;2016&#95;25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gupta_2016-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A specific relationship between vertebrates and <a href="/wiki/Tunicate" title="Tunicate">tunicates</a> is supported by two molecular markers, the proteins <a href="/wiki/Rrp44" class="mw-redirect" title="Rrp44">Rrp44</a> (associated with the <a href="/wiki/Exosome_complex" title="Exosome complex">exosome complex</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Serine_C-palmitoyltransferase" title="Serine C-palmitoyltransferase">serine C-palmitoyltransferase</a>. These are exclusively shared by species from these two subphyla, but not by cephalochordates.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gupta&#95;2016&#95;25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gupta_2016-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Evolutionary_history">Evolutionary history</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Evolutionary history"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cambrian_explosion:_first_craniates">Cambrian explosion: first craniates</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Cambrian explosion: first craniates"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cambrian_explosion" title="Cambrian explosion">Cambrian explosion</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Haikouichthys_cropped.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Haikouichthys_cropped.jpg/250px-Haikouichthys_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="83" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Haikouichthys_cropped.jpg/500px-Haikouichthys_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="568" data-file-height="205" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Cambrian" title="Cambrian">Cambrian</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Haikouichthys" title="Haikouichthys">Haikouichthys</a></i>, 518 <a href="/wiki/Myr" class="mw-redirect" title="Myr">mya</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Shu&#95;2003&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shu_2003-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>Vertebrates originated during the <a href="/wiki/Cambrian_explosion" title="Cambrian explosion">Cambrian explosion</a> at the start of the Paleozoic, which saw a rise in animal diversity. The earliest known vertebrates belong to the <a href="/wiki/Chengjiang_biota" class="mw-redirect" title="Chengjiang biota">Chengjiang biota</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Shu1999&#95;27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shu1999-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and lived about 518 million years ago.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Yang2018&#95;1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yang2018-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These include <i><a href="/wiki/Haikouichthys" title="Haikouichthys">Haikouichthys</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Myllokunmingia" title="Myllokunmingia">Myllokunmingia</a></i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Shu1999&#95;27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shu1999-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Zhongjianichthys" title="Zhongjianichthys">Zhongjianichthys</a></i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Shu&#95;2003&#95;26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shu_2003-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and probably <i><a href="/wiki/Yunnanozoon" title="Yunnanozoon">Yunnanozoon</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Unlike other Cambrian animals, these groups had the basic vertebrate body plan: a notochord, rudimentary vertebrae, and a well-defined head and tail, but lacked jaws.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As such, one perspective is that <i>Haikouichthys</i> and other <a href="/wiki/Myllokunmingiidae" title="Myllokunmingiidae">Myllokunmingiidae</a> probably represent basal <a href="/wiki/Stem_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Stem group">stem group</a> craniates rather than actual vertebrates.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Shu2003&#95;30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shu2003-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A vertebrate group of uncertain phylogeny, small eel-like <a href="/wiki/Conodont" title="Conodont">conodonts</a>, are known from <a href="/wiki/Microfossil" title="Microfossil">microfossils</a> of their paired tooth segments from the late Cambrian to the end of the Triassic.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Zoologists have debated whether teeth <a href="/wiki/Mineralized_tissues" title="Mineralized tissues">mineralized</a> first, given the hard teeth of the soft-bodied conodonts, and then bones, or vice versa, but it seems that the mineralized skeleton came first.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Murdock&#95;Dong&#95;2013&#95;32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murdock_Dong_2013-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Paleozoic:_evolution_of_fish,_first_amphibians"><span id="Paleozoic:_evolution_of_fish.2C_first_amphibians"></span>Paleozoic: evolution of fish, first amphibians</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Paleozoic: evolution of fish, first amphibians"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_fish" title="Evolution of fish">Evolution of fish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_tetrapods" title="Evolution of tetrapods">Evolution of tetrapods</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Acanthostega_BW.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Acanthostega_BW.jpg/250px-Acanthostega_BW.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="87" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Acanthostega_BW.jpg/500px-Acanthostega_BW.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="302" /></a><figcaption><i><a href="/wiki/Acanthostega" title="Acanthostega">Acanthostega</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a> <a href="/wiki/Labyrinthodontia" title="Labyrinthodontia">labyrinthodont</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 365 mya<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> </figcaption></figure>
<p>The first <a href="/wiki/Gnathostomata" title="Gnathostomata">jawed vertebrates</a> may have appeared in the late <a href="/wiki/Ordovician" title="Ordovician">Ordovician</a> (~445 mya) or <a href="/wiki/Silurian" title="Silurian">Silurian</a>, and became common in the <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian period</a>, often known as the "Age of Fishes".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-britannica1954&#95;34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica1954-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The  <a href="/wiki/Bony_fishes" class="mw-redirect" title="Bony fishes">bony fishes</a> appeared in the Silurian; they became common in the Devonian.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the middle of the Devonian, a lineage of bony fishes, the <a href="/wiki/Sarcopterygii" title="Sarcopterygii">sarcopterygii</a>, with both gills and air-breathing lungs adapted to life in swampy pools, used their muscular paired fins to propel themselves on land.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Carroll&#95;1977&#95;36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll_1977-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The fins, already possessing bones and joints, evolved into the two pairs of walking legs of the first <a href="/wiki/Tetrapods" class="mw-redirect" title="Tetrapods">tetrapods</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-NarkiewiczNarkiewicz2015&#95;37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NarkiewiczNarkiewicz2015-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Famennian" title="Famennian">Famennian</a> stage of the <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These tetrapods established themselves on land as <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a> in the next geological period, the <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous">Carboniferous</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A group of vertebrates, the <a href="/wiki/Amniote" title="Amniote">amniotes</a>, with membranes around the <a href="/wiki/Embryo" title="Embryo">embryo</a> allowing it to survive on dry land, branched from amphibious tetrapods in the Carboniferous.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-benton2014&#95;40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-benton2014-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Mesozoic:_Dinosaurs_and_other_land_animals">Mesozoic: Dinosaurs and other land animals</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mesozoic: Dinosaurs and other land animals"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperodapedon_BW2_white_background.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hyperodapedon_BW2_white_background.jpg/250px-Hyperodapedon_BW2_white_background.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="94" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hyperodapedon_BW2_white_background.jpg/500px-Hyperodapedon_BW2_white_background.jpg 2x" data-file-width="613" data-file-height="250" /></a><figcaption><i><a href="/wiki/Hyperodapedon" title="Hyperodapedon">Hyperodapedon</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Diapsid" title="Diapsid">diapsid</a> reptile of the <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 230 mya</figcaption></figure>
<p>At the onset of the Mesozoic, all larger vertebrate groups were devastated after the <a href="/wiki/Permian-Triassic_extinction_event" class="mw-redirect" title="Permian-Triassic extinction event">largest mass extinction in earth history</a>. The following <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">recovery phase</a> saw the emergence of many new vertebrate groups that are still around today, and this time has been described as the origin of modern ecosystems. On the continents, the ancestors of modern <a href="/wiki/Lissamphibia" title="Lissamphibia">lissamphibians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turtle" title="Turtle">turtles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crocodilia" title="Crocodilia">crocodilians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lizard" title="Lizard">lizards</a>, and mammals appeared, as well as <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">dinosaurs</a>, which gave rise to birds later in the Mesozoic. In the seas, various groups of marine reptiles evolved, as did new groups of fish.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-benton2014&#95;40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-benton2014-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the end of the Mesozoic, <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous%E2%80%93Paleogene_extinction_event" title="Cretaceous–Paleogene extinction event">another extinction event</a> extirpated dinosaurs (other than birds) and many other vertebrate groups.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Fortey&#95;1999&#95;41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortey_1999-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cenozoic:_Age_of_Mammals">Cenozoic: Age of Mammals</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cenozoic: Age of Mammals"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Fossil_bird_(Green_River_Formation,_Lower_Eocene;_Fossil_Lake_Basin,_southwestern_Wyoming,_USA)_(15529177925).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Fossil_bird_%28Green_River_Formation%2C_Lower_Eocene%3B_Fossil_Lake_Basin%2C_southwestern_Wyoming%2C_USA%29_%2815529177925%29.jpg/250px-Fossil_bird_%28Green_River_Formation%2C_Lower_Eocene%3B_Fossil_Lake_Basin%2C_southwestern_Wyoming%2C_USA%29_%2815529177925%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="152" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Fossil_bird_%28Green_River_Formation%2C_Lower_Eocene%3B_Fossil_Lake_Basin%2C_southwestern_Wyoming%2C_USA%29_%2815529177925%29.jpg/330px-Fossil_bird_%28Green_River_Formation%2C_Lower_Eocene%3B_Fossil_Lake_Basin%2C_southwestern_Wyoming%2C_USA%29_%2815529177925%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2624" data-file-height="2664" /></a><figcaption><i><a href="/wiki/Nahmavis" title="Nahmavis">Nahmavis</a></i>, an <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">Eocene</a> bird, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 50 mya</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cenozoic" title="Cenozoic">Cenozoic</a>, the current era, is sometimes called the "Age of Mammals", because of the dominance of the terrestrial environment by that group. <a href="/wiki/Placental_mammals" class="mw-redirect" title="Placental mammals">Placental mammals</a> have predominantly occupied the Northern Hemisphere, with <a href="/wiki/Marsupial" title="Marsupial">marsupial mammals</a> in the Southern Hemisphere.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Approaches_to_classification">Approaches to classification</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Approaches to classification"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Taxonomic_history">Taxonomic history</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Taxonomic history"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Vertebrata">Vertebrata</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Vertebrata"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Owen%27s_archetype.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Owen%27s_archetype.jpg/250px-Owen%27s_archetype.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Owen%27s_archetype.jpg/500px-Owen%27s_archetype.jpg 2x" data-file-width="682" data-file-height="327" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Richard_Owen" title="Richard Owen">Sir Richard Owen's</a> 1847 illustration of the archetypal vertebrate skeleton</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1801, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Lamarck" title="Jean-Baptiste Lamarck">Jean-Baptiste Lamarck</a> defined the vertebrates as a taxonomic group,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Nielsen2012&#95;2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nielsen2012-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Phylum" title="Phylum">phylum</a> distinct from the <a href="/wiki/Invertebrate" title="Invertebrate">invertebrates</a> he was studying.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Irie&#95;2018&#95;44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irie_2018-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He described them as consisting of four classes, namely fish, reptiles, birds, and mammals,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but treated the <a href="/wiki/Cephalochordate" class="mw-redirect" title="Cephalochordate">cephalochordates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunicate" title="Tunicate">tunicates</a> as <a href="/wiki/Mollusca" title="Mollusca">molluscs</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Irie&#95;2018&#95;44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irie_2018-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1866, <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Haeckel" title="Ernst Haeckel">Ernst Haeckel</a> called both his Craniata (vertebrates) and his Acrania (cephalochordates) Vertebrata.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Irie&#95;2018&#95;44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irie_2018-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1877, <a href="/wiki/Ray_Lankester" title="Ray Lankester">Ray Lankester</a> grouped the craniates, cephalochordates, and urochordates (tunicates) as Vertebrata.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Irie&#95;2018&#95;44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irie_2018-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1880–1881, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Maitland_Balfour" title="Francis Maitland Balfour">Francis Maitland Balfour</a> placed the Vertebrata as a subphylum within the chordates.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Irie&#95;2018&#95;44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irie_2018-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2018, Naoki Irie and colleagues proposed making Vertebrata a full phylum.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Irie&#95;2018&#95;44-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irie_2018-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Cyclostomes_and_craniates">Cyclostomes and craniates</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Cyclostomes and craniates"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 1758, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus" title="Carl Linnaeus">Linnaeus</a> classified hagfishes as <a href="/wiki/Vermes" title="Vermes">Vermes</a>, not vertebrates.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
In 1806, <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Marie_Constant_Dum%C3%A9ril" title="André Marie Constant Duméril">André Marie Constant Duméril</a> grouped hagfishes and lampreys in the taxon Cyclostomi, characterized by horny teeth borne on a tongue-like apparatus, a large notochord as adults, and pouch-shaped gills (Marsupibranchii). The cyclostomes were seen as either degenerate cartilaginous fishes or primitive vertebrates.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Janvier&#95;47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janvier-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1889, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Drinker_Cope" title="Edward Drinker Cope">Edward Drinker Cope</a> coined the name <a href="/wiki/Agnatha" title="Agnatha">Agnatha</a> ("jawless") for a group that included the cyclostomes and fossil groups in which jaws could not be observed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Janvier&#95;47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janvier-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Vertebrates were subsequently divided into two major sister-groups: the Agnatha and the Gnathostomata (jawed vertebrates). In 1927, <a href="/wiki/Erik_Stensi%C3%B6" title="Erik Stensiö">Erik Stensiö</a> suggested that the two groups of living agnathans (i.e. the cyclostomes) arose independently from fossil agnathans.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Janvier&#95;47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janvier-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
In 1977, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B8ren_L%C3%B8vtrup" title="Søren Løvtrup">Søren Løvtrup</a> argued that lampreys are more closely related to gnathostomes, based on characters such as radial muscles in the fins, true lymphocytes, neuromasts in the inner ear, and a cerebellum. This implied that Vertebrata and Craniata were distinct taxa.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Janvier&#95;47-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janvier-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The validity of the taxon "Craniata" was examined in 2002 by Delarbre et al. using <a href="/wiki/MtDNA" class="mw-redirect" title="MtDNA">mtDNA</a> sequencing, concluding that Myxini is more closely related to <a href="/wiki/Hyperoartia" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperoartia">Hyperoartia</a> than to Gnathostomata - i.e., that modern jawless fishes form a clade called <a href="/wiki/Cyclostomata" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyclostomata">Cyclostomata</a>. This implies that Vertebrata should return to its old content (<a href="/wiki/Gnathostomata" title="Gnathostomata">Gnathostomata</a> + <a href="/wiki/Cyclostomata" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyclostomata">Cyclostomata</a>) and the name Craniata is a junior synonym of Vertebrata.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2010, the debate concluded when the French paleontologist <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Janvier" title="Philippe Janvier">Philippe Janvier</a> stated that he accepted that both vertebrates and cyclostomes were monophyletic, and that "the intuitions of 19th century zoologists were correct in assuming that [cyclostomes] (notably, hagfishes) are strongly degenerate and have lost many characters over time."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Janvier&#95;2010&#95;49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janvier_2010-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Traditional_taxonomy">Traditional taxonomy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Traditional taxonomy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Fish_evolution.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Fish_evolution.png/500px-Fish_evolution.png" decoding="async" width="340" height="243" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Fish_evolution.png/960px-Fish_evolution.png 2x" data-file-width="1073" data-file-height="767" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">Diversity</a> of various groups of vertebrates through the <a href="/wiki/Geologic_ages" class="mw-redirect" title="Geologic ages">geologic ages</a>. The width of the bubbles signifies the number of <a href="/wiki/Family_(biology)" title="Family (biology)">families</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Conventional <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_taxonomy" title="Evolutionary taxonomy">evolutionary taxonomy</a> groups <a href="/wiki/Extant_taxon" class="mw-redirect" title="Extant taxon">extant</a> vertebrates into seven classes based on traditional interpretations of gross <a href="/wiki/Anatomy" title="Anatomy">anatomical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">physiological</a> traits. The commonly held classification lists three classes of fish and four of <a href="/wiki/Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod">tetrapods</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Campbell&#95;50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This ignores some of the natural relationships between the groupings. For example, the birds derive from a group of reptiles, so "<a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">Reptilia</a>" excluding <a href="/wiki/Aves" class="mw-redirect" title="Aves">Aves</a> is not <a href="/wiki/Clade" title="Clade">a natural grouping</a>; it is described as <a href="/wiki/Paraphyly" title="Paraphyly">paraphyletic</a> and shown in quotation marks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b>Subphylum Vertebrata</b>
<ul><li>Class "<a href="/wiki/Agnatha" title="Agnatha">Agnatha</a>" (jawless fishes)</li>
<li>Class <a href="/wiki/Chondrichthyes" title="Chondrichthyes">Chondrichthyes</a> (cartilaginous fishes)</li>
<li>Class "<a href="/wiki/Osteichthyes" title="Osteichthyes">Osteichthyes</a>" (bony fishes)</li>
<li>Class "<a href="/wiki/Amphibia" class="mw-redirect" title="Amphibia">Amphibia</a>" (traditional amphibians)</li>
<li>Class "<a href="/wiki/Reptilia" class="mw-redirect" title="Reptilia">Reptilia</a>" (reptiles)</li>
<li>Class <a href="/wiki/Aves" class="mw-redirect" title="Aves">Aves</a> (birds)</li>
<li>Class <a href="/wiki/Mammalia" class="mw-redirect" title="Mammalia">Mammalia</a> (mammals)</li></ul></li></ul>
<p>In addition to these, there are two classes of extinct armoured fishes, <a href="/wiki/Placodermi" class="mw-redirect" title="Placodermi">Placodermi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acanthodii" title="Acanthodii">Acanthodii</a>.
</p><p>Other ways of classifying the vertebrates have been devised, particularly with emphasis on the <a href="/wiki/Phylogeny" class="mw-redirect" title="Phylogeny">phylogeny</a> of <a href="/wiki/Labyrinthodontia" title="Labyrinthodontia">early amphibians</a> and reptiles. An example based on work by M.J. Benton in 2004<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Benton2004&#95;53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benton2004-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is given here († = <a href="/wiki/Extinct" class="mw-redirect" title="Extinct">extinct</a>, "" = paraphyletic):
</p>
<ul><li><b>Subphylum Vertebrata</b>
<ul><li><b>Infraphylum "<a href="/wiki/Agnatha" title="Agnatha">Agnatha</a>"</b> (<a href="/wiki/Lamprey" title="Lamprey">lampreys</a> and other jawless fishes)
<ul><li><b>Superclass <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr><a href="/wiki/Anaspidomorphi" title="Anaspidomorphi">Anaspidomorphi</a></b> (anaspids and relatives)
<ul><li>Class <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr><a href="/wiki/Anaspida" title="Anaspida">Anaspida</a> (anaspids)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Superclass <a href="/wiki/Cyclostomi" title="Cyclostomi">Cyclostomata</a></b> (cyclostomes)
<ul><li>Class <a href="/wiki/Hagfish" title="Hagfish">Myxini</a> (hagfish)</li>
<li>Class <a href="/wiki/Lamprey" title="Lamprey">Petromyzontida</a> (lampreys)</li></ul></li>
<li>Class <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr><a href="/wiki/Cephalaspidomorphi" title="Cephalaspidomorphi">Cephalaspidomorphi</a> (cephalaspidomorphs)</li>
<li>Class <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr><a href="/wiki/Conodont" title="Conodont">Conodonta</a> (conodonts)</li>
<li>Class <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr><a href="/wiki/Pteraspidomorphi" class="mw-redirect" title="Pteraspidomorphi">Pteraspidomorpha</a> (pteraspidomorphs)</li>
<li>Class <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr><a href="/wiki/Thelodonti" title="Thelodonti">Thelodonti</a> (thelodonts)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Infraphylum <a href="/wiki/Gnathostomata" title="Gnathostomata">Gnathostomata</a></b> (vertebrates with jaws)
<ul><li>Class <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr>"<a href="/wiki/Placodermi" class="mw-redirect" title="Placodermi">Placodermi</a>" (armoured fishes)</li>
<li>Class <a href="/wiki/Chondrichthyes" title="Chondrichthyes">Chondrichthyes</a> (cartilaginous fishes)</li>
<li>Class <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr>"<a href="/wiki/Acanthodii" title="Acanthodii">Acanthodii</a>" (spiny 'sharks')</li>
<li><b>"<a href="/wiki/Osteichthyes" title="Osteichthyes">Osteichthyes</a>"</b> (bony fishes)
<ul><li>Class <a href="/wiki/Actinopterygii" title="Actinopterygii">Actinopterygii</a> (ray-finned bony fishes)</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Sarcopterygii" title="Sarcopterygii">Sarcopterygii</a>" (lobe-finned fishes, <a href="/wiki/Cladistics" title="Cladistics">cladistically</a> including the <a href="/wiki/Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod">tetrapods</a>)
<ul><li><b>Superclass <a href="/wiki/Tetrapoda" class="mw-redirect" title="Tetrapoda">Tetrapoda</a></b> (four-limbed vertebrates)
<ul><li>Class "<a href="/wiki/Amphibia" class="mw-redirect" title="Amphibia">Amphibia</a>" (amphibians, <a href="/wiki/Lissamphibia" title="Lissamphibia">Lissamphibia</a>)</li>
<li>Class <a href="/wiki/Synapsida" title="Synapsida">Synapsida</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mammals" class="mw-redirect" title="Mammals">mammals</a> and their extinct relatives)</li>
<li>Class <a href="/wiki/Sauropsida" title="Sauropsida">Sauropsida</a> (modern reptiles and <a href="/wiki/Birds" class="mw-redirect" title="Birds">birds</a>)</li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Incertae_sedis" title="Incertae sedis">Incertae sedis</a></b></i>
<ul><li>Genus <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr><i><a href="/wiki/Nuucichthys" title="Nuucichthys">Nuucichthys</a></i></li>
<li>Genus <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr><i><a href="/wiki/Palaeospondylus" title="Palaeospondylus">Palaeospondylus</a></i></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul>
<p>While this traditional taxonomy is orderly, most of the groups are paraphyletic, meaning that the structure does not accurately reflect the natural evolved grouping.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Benton2004&#95;53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benton2004-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For instance, descendants of the first reptiles include modern reptiles, mammals and birds; the agnathans have given rise to the jawed vertebrates; the <a href="/wiki/Osteichthyes" title="Osteichthyes">bony fishes</a> have given rise to the <a href="/wiki/Tetrapoda" class="mw-redirect" title="Tetrapoda">land vertebrates</a>; a group of amphibians, the <a href="/wiki/Labyrinthodont" class="mw-redirect" title="Labyrinthodont">labyrinthodonts</a>, have given rise to the <a href="/wiki/Reptilia" class="mw-redirect" title="Reptilia">reptiles</a> (traditionally including the mammal-like synapsids), which in turn have given rise to the mammals and birds. Most scientists working with vertebrates use a classification based purely on phylogeny, organized by their known evolutionary history.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Irie&#95;2018&#95;44-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irie_2018-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="External_phylogeny">External phylogeny</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: External phylogeny"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The closest relatives of vertebrates have been debated over the years. It was once thought that the <a href="/wiki/Cephalochordata" class="mw-redirect" title="Cephalochordata">Cephalochordata</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Sister_taxon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sister taxon">sister taxon</a> to Vertebrata. This group, Notochordata, was taken to be sister to the <a href="/wiki/Tunicata" class="mw-redirect" title="Tunicata">Tunicata</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since 2006, analysis has shown that the tunicates + vertebrates form a clade, the Olfactores, with Cephalochordata as its sister (the <a href="/wiki/Olfactores#Olfactores_hypothesis" title="Olfactores">Olfactores hypothesis</a>), as shown in the following <a href="/wiki/Phylogenetic_tree" title="Phylogenetic tree">phylogenetic tree</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Delsuc&#95;2006&#95;55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Delsuc_2006-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Dunn&#95;2008&#95;56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dunn_2008-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Gupta&#95;2016&#95;25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gupta_2016-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Internal_phylogeny">Internal phylogeny</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Internal phylogeny"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

<p><a href="/wiki/Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur">Dinosaurs</a> <span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Spot-billed_pelican_takeoff_white_background.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Spot-billed_pelican_takeoff_white_background.jpg/60px-Spot-billed_pelican_takeoff_white_background.jpg" decoding="async" width="60" height="62" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Spot-billed_pelican_takeoff_white_background.jpg/120px-Spot-billed_pelican_takeoff_white_background.jpg 2x" data-file-width="830" data-file-height="858" /></a></span>
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="clade-slabel last">
</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
</td></tr>

<td class="clade-slabel last">

</td></tr>

<td class="clade-slabel last">

<tr>
<td class="clade-slabel last">(scaly&#160;skin)
</td></tr></tbody></table></div>

</td></tr></tbody></table></div>

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="clade-slabel last">(bony&#160;fishes)
</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
</td></tr>

<td class="clade-slabel last">(jawed)
</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="clade-slabel last">(backbone)
</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p>The placement of hagfishes within the vertebrates has been controversial. Their lack of proper vertebrae (among other characteristics of jawless lampreys and jawed vertebrates) led authors of phylogenetic analyses based on <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(biology)" title="Morphology (biology)">morphology</a> to place them outside Vertebrata.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Molecular_data" class="mw-redirect" title="Molecular data">Molecular data</a> however indicates that they are vertebrates, being most closely related to lampreys.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-hagfish&#95;60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hagfish-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> An older view is that they are a sister group of vertebrates in the common taxon of Craniata.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2019, Tetsuto Miyashita and colleagues reconciled the two types of analysis, supporting the <a href="/wiki/Cyclostomata" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyclostomata">Cyclostomata</a> hypothesis using only morphological data.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A wider issue is the position of fossil agnathans, such as the Myllokunmingiida. Tetsuto Miyashita and colleagues in 2019 place them tentatively as part of the Vertebrata total group, outside the Vertebrata crown group that led to all extant vertebrates. These fossils have a cranium (a skull of bone or cartilage) but at most a rudimentary vertebral column, so they can be viewed as part of a craniate clade that also includes the crown group vertebrates which possess a full vertebral column.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Miyashita&#95;Coates&#95;2019&#95;64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miyashita_Coates_2019-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Diversity">Diversity</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Diversity"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Species_by_group">Species by group</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Species by group"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Described and extant vertebrate species are split roughly evenly but non-phylogenetically between non-tetrapod "fish" and <a href="/wiki/Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod">tetrapods</a>. The following table lists the number of described <a href="/wiki/Extant_taxa" class="mw-redirect" title="Extant taxa">extant</a> species for each vertebrate <a href="/wiki/Class_(biology)" title="Class (biology)">class</a> as estimated in the <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List_of_Threatened_Species" class="mw-redirect" title="IUCN Red List of Threatened Species">IUCN Red List of Threatened Species</a>, 2014.3.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-IUCN1014&#95;65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN1014-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Paraphyletic groups are shown in quotation marks.
</p>

<td><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Cuvier-97-Canard_colvert.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Cuvier-97-Canard_colvert.jpg/120px-Cuvier-97-Canard_colvert.jpg" decoding="async" width="70" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Cuvier-97-Canard_colvert.jpg/250px-Cuvier-97-Canard_colvert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="625" data-file-height="346" /></a></span>
</td>
<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">Aves</a>
<p><small>(birds)</small>
</p>
</td>
<td align="center">10,425
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="6" align="right"><b>Total described species</b>
</td>
<td align="center"><b>66,178</b>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The IUCN estimates that 1,305,075 <a href="/wiki/Invertebrate#Number_of_extant_species" title="Invertebrate">extant invertebrate species</a> have been described,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-IUCN1014&#95;65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN1014-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which means that less than 5% of the <a href="/wiki/Animal#Number_of_extant_species" title="Animal">described animal species</a> in the world are vertebrates.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Zhang2013&#95;67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zhang2013-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Recent_population_trends">Recent population trends</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vertebrate&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Recent population trends"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Living_Planet_Index" title="Living Planet Index">Living Planet Index</a>, following 16,704 populations of 4,005 species of vertebrates, shows a decline of 60% between 1970 and 2014.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since 1970, freshwater species declined 83%, and tropical populations in South and Central America declined 89%.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The authors note that "An average trend in population change is not an average of total numbers of animals lost."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a>, this could lead to a sixth <a href="/wiki/Extinction_event" title="Extinction event">major extinction event</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The five main causes of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_loss" title="Biodiversity loss">biodiversity loss</a> are <a href="/wiki/Land-use_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Land-use change">land-use change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Overexploitation" title="Overexploitation">overexploitation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive species</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references" data-mw-group="lower-alpha">
<li id="cite&#95;note-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-58">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Agnatha as traditionally defined is paraphyletic, that is, a taxon including all jawless fishes, but if one only includes living species then the group becomes monophyletic and equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Cyclostomi" title="Cyclostomi">Cyclostomi</a>.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
